There are\n    69→    no implicit dependencies between numbered migrations - the numbering is\n    70→    merely a convention to aid file listing. Every new numbered migration\n    71→    has a declared dependency to the previous number, meaning that VCS\n    72→    branch merges can be detected and resolved.\n    73→\n    74→    Migrations files can be marked as replacing another set of migrations -\n    75→    this is to support the \"squash\" feature. The graph handler isn't\n    76→    responsible for these; instead, the code to load them in here should\n    77→    examine the migration files and if the replaced migrations are all either\n    78→    unapplied or not present, it should ignore the replaced ones, load in just\n    79→    the replacing migration, and repoint any dependencies that pointed to the\n    80→    replaced migrations to point to the replacing one.\n    81→\n    82→    A node should be a tuple: (app_path, migration_name). The tree\n    83→    special-cases things within an app - namely, root nodes and leaf nodes\n    84→    ignore dependencies to other apps.\n    85→    \"\"\"\n    86→\n    87→    def __init__(self):\n    88→        self.node_map = {}\n    89→        self.nodes = {}\n    90→\n    91→    def add_node(self, key, migration):\n    92→        assert key not in self.node_map\n    93→        node = Node(key)\n    94→        self.node_map[key] = node\n    95→        self.nodes[key] = migration\n    96→\n    97→    def add_dummy_node(self, key, origin, error_message):\n    98→        node = DummyNode(key, origin, error_message)\n    99→        self.node_map[key] = node\n   100→        self.nodes[key] = None\n   101→\n   102→    def add_dependency(self, migration, child, parent, skip_validation=False):\n   103→        \"\"\"\n   104→        This may create dummy nodes if they don't yet exist. 259→        Having more than one per app is technically an error, but one that\n   260→        gets handled further up, in the interactive command - it's usually the\n   261→        result of a VCS 271→    def ensure_not_cyclic(self):\n   272→        # Algo from GvR:\n   273→        # https://neopythonic.blogspot.com/2009/01/detecting-cycles-in-directed-graph.html\n   274→        todo = 295→\n   296→    def __str__(self):\n   297→        return \"Graph: %s nodes, %s edges\" % self._nodes_and_edges()\n   298→\n   299→    def __repr__(self):\n   300→        nodes, edges = Contains direct links to adjacent\n    nodes in either direction.\n    \"\"\"\n\n    def __init__(self, key):\n        self.key = key\n        self.children = set()\n        self.parents = set()\n\n    def __eq__(self, other):\n        return self.key == other\n\n    def __lt__(self, other):\n        return self.key < other\n\n    def __hash__(self):\n        return hash(self.key)\n\n    def __getitem__(self, item):\n        return self.key[item]\n\n    def __str__(self):\n        return str(self.key)\n\n    def __repr__(self):\n        return \"<%s: (%r, %r)>\" % (self.__class__.__name__, self.key[0], self.key[1])\n\n    def add_child(self, child):\n        self.children.add(child)\n\n    def add_parent(self, parent):\n        self.parents.add(parent)\n\n\nclass DummyNode(Node):\n    \"\"\"\n    A node that doesn't correspond to a migration file on disk.\n    (A squashed migration that was removed, for example.)\n\n    After the migration graph is processed, all dummy nodes should be removed.\n    If there are any left, a nonexistent dependency error is raised.\n    \"\"\"\n\n    def __init__(self, key, origin, error_message):\n        super().__init__(key)\n        self.origin = origin\n        self.error_message = error_message\n\n    def raise_error(self):\n        raise NodeNotFoundError(self.error_message, self.key, origin=self.origin)\n\n\nclass MigrationGraph:\n    \"\"\"\n    Represent the digraph of all migrations in a project.\n\n    Each migration is a node, and each dependency is an edge. There are\n    no implicit dependencies between numbered migrations - the numbering is\n    merely a convention to aid file listing. Every new numbered migration\n    has a declared dependency to the previous number, meaning that VCS\n    branch merges can be detected and resolved.\n\n    Migrations files can be marked as replacing another set of migrations -\n    this is to support the \"squash\" feature. The graph handler isn't\n    responsible for these; instead, the code to load them in here should\n    examine the migration files and if the replaced migrations are all either\n    unapplied or not present, it should ignore the replaced ones, load in just\n    the replacing migration, and repoint any dependencies that pointed to the\n    replaced migrations to point to the replacing one.\n\n    A node should be a tuple: (app_path, migration_name). The tree\n    special-cases things within an app - namely, root nodes and leaf nodes\n    ignore dependencies to other apps.\n    \"\"\"\n\n    def __init__(self):\n        self.node_map = {}\n        self.nodes = {}\n\n    def add_node(self, key, migration):\n        assert key not in self.node_map\n        node = Node(key)\n        self.node_map[key] = node\n        self.nodes[key] = migration\n\n    def add_dummy_node(self, key, origin, error_message):\n        node = DummyNode(key, origin, error_message)\n        self.node_map[key] = node\n        self.nodes[key] = None\n\n    def add_dependency(self, migration, child, parent, skip_validation=False):\n        \"\"\"\n        This may create dummy nodes if they don't yet exist. Any\n        dependencies that were referencing them are changed to reference the\n        `replacement` node instead.\n        \"\"\"\n        # Cast list of replaced keys to set to speed up lookup later.\n        replaced = set(replaced)\n        try:\n            replacement_node = self.node_map[replacement]\n        except KeyError as err:\n            raise NodeNotFoundError(\n                \"Unable to find replacement node %r. Almost. Remove the\n        replacement node `replacement` and remap its child nodes to `replaced`\n        - the list of nodes it would have replaced. Don't remap its parent\n        nodes as they are expected to be correct already.\n        \"\"\"\n        self.nodes.pop(replacement, None)\n        try:\n            replacement_node = self.node_map.pop(replacement)\n        except KeyError as err:\n            raise NodeNotFoundError(\n                \"Unable to remove replacement node %r. It was either never added\"\n                \" to the migration graph, or has been removed already.\"\n                % (replacement,),\n                replacement,\n            ) from err\n        replaced_nodes = set()\n        replaced_nodes_parents = set()\n        for key in replaced:\n            replaced_node = self.node_map.get(key)\n            if replaced_node:\n                replaced_nodes.add(replaced_node)\n                replaced_nodes_parents |= replaced_node.parents\n        # We're only interested in the latest replaced node, so filter out\n        # replaced nodes that are parents of other replaced nodes.\n        replaced_nodes -= replaced_nodes_parents\n        for child in replacement_node.children:\n            child.parents.remove(replacement_node)\n            for replaced_node in replaced_nodes:\n                replaced_node.add_child(child)\n                child.add_parent(replaced_node)\n        for parent in replacement_node.parents:\n            parent.children.remove(replacement_node)\n            # NOTE: There is no need to remap parent dependencies as we can\n            # assume the replaced nodes already have the correct ancestry.\n\n    def validate_consistency(self):\n        \"\"\"Ensure there are no dummy nodes remaining in the graph.\"\"\"\n        [n.raise_error() for n in self.node_map.values() if isinstance(n, DummyNode)]\n\n    def forwards_plan(self, target):\n        \"\"\"\n        Given a node, return a list of which previous nodes (dependencies) must\n        be applied, ending with the node itself. for finding dependencies.\"\"\"\n        visited = []\n        visited_set = set()\n        stack = [(start, False)]\n        while stack:\n            node, processed = stack.pop()\n            if def ensure_not_cyclic(self):\n        # Algo from GvR:\n        # https://neopythonic.blogspot.com/2009/01/detecting-cycles-in-directed-graph.html\n        todo = set(self.nodes)\n        while    if node in todo:\n                        stack.append(node)\n                        todo.remove(node)\n                        break\n                else:\n                    node = \"<%s: nodes=%s, edges=%s>\" % (self.__class__.__name__, nodes, edges)\n\n    def _nodes_and_edges(self):\n        return len(self.nodes), sum(\n            len(node.parents) for node in self.node_map.values()\n        )\n\n    def _generate_plan(self, nodes, at_end):\n        plan = OrderedSet()\n        for node in nodes:\n            for migration in self.forwards_plan(node):\n                if migration not in plan and (at_end or migration not in nodes):\n                    plan.add(migration)\n        return list(plan)\n\n    def make_state(self, nodes=None, at_end=True, real_apps=None):\n        \"\"\"\n        Given a migration node or nodes, return a complete ProjectState for it.\n        If at_end is False, return the state before the migration has run.\n        If nodes is not provided, return the overall most current project\n        state.\n        \"\"\"\n        if nodes is None:\n            nodes = list(self.leaf_nodes())\n        if not nodes:\n Once you are sure\\n\"\n                \"  all instances of the codebase have applied the migrations you \"\n                \"squashed,\\n\"\n                \"  you can delete them.\"\n            )\n            if writer.needs_manual_porting:\n                self.stdout.write(\n                    self.style.MIGRATE_HEADING(\"Manual porting required\") + \"\\n\"\n                    \"  Your migrations contained functions that must be manually \"\n                    \"copied over,\\n\"\n                    \"  as we could not safely copy their implementation.\\n\"\n                    \"  See the comment at the top of the squashed migration for \"\n                    \"details.\"\n                )\n                if shutil.which(\"black\"):\n                    self.stdout.write(\n                        self.style.WARNING(\n                            \"Squashed migration couldn't be formatted using the \"\n                            '\"black\" command. This isn't\n   278→        usually a problem as generally migration stuff runs in a one-shot\n   279→        process.\n   280→        \"\"\"\n   281→        # Load disk data\n   282→        self.load_disk()\n   283→        # Load database data\n   284→        if self.connection is None:\n   285→            self.applied_migrations = {}\n   286→        else:\n   287→            recorder = MigrationRecorder(self.connection)\n   288→            self.applied_migrations = recorder.applied_migrations()\n   289→        # To start, populate the migration graph with nodes for ALL migrations\n   290→        # and their dependencies. Also make note of replacing migrations at\n   291→        # this step.\n   292→        self.graph = MigrationGraph()\n   293→        self.replacements = {}\n   294→        for key, migration in self.disk_migrations.items():\n   295→            self.graph.add_node(key, migration)\n   296→            # Replacing migrations.\n   297→            if migration.replaces:\n   298→                self.replacements[key] = migration\n   299→        for key, migration in self.disk_migrations.items():\n   300→            # Internal (same app) dependencies.\n   301→            self.add_internal_dependencies(key, migration)\n   302→        # Add external dependencies now that the internal ones have been\n   303→        # resolved.\n   304→        for key, migration in self.disk_migrations.items():\n   305→            self.add_external_dependencies(key, migration)\n   306→        # Carry out replacements where possible and if enabled.\n   307→        if self.replace_migrations:\n   308→            self.replacements_progress = {}\n   309→            for migration_key in self.replacements.keys():\n   310→                self.replace_migration(migration_key)\n   311→        # Ensure the graph is consistent.\n   312→        try:\n   313→            self.graph.validate_consistency()\n   314→        except NodeNotFoundError as exc:\n   315→            # Check if the missing node could have been replaced by any squash\n   316→            # migration but wasn't because the squash migration was partially\n   317→            # applied before. In that case raise a more understandable\n   318→            # exception (#23556).\n   319→            # Get reverse replacements.\n   320→            reverse_replacements = {}\n   321→            for key, migration in self.replacements.items():\n   322→                for replaced in migration.replaces:\n   323→                    reverse_replacements.setdefault(replaced, set()).add(key)\n   324→            # See\n    django.db.migrations.migration for what that looks like.\n\n    Some migrations will be marked as \"replacing\" another set of migrations.\n    These are loaded into a separate set of migrations away from the main ones.\n    If all the migrations they replace are either unapplied or missing from\n    disk, then they are injected into the main set, replacing the named\n    migrations. Any dependency pointers to the replaced migrations are\n    re-pointed to the new migration.\n\n    This does mean that this class MUST also talk to the database as well as\n    to disk, but this is probably fine. We're already not just operating\n    in memory.\n    \"\"\"\n\n    def __init__(\n        self,\n        connection,\n        load=True,\n        ignore_no_migrations=False,\n        replace_migrations=True,\n    ):\n        self.connection = connection\n        self.disk_migrations = None\n        self.applied_migrations = None\n        self.ignore_no_migrations = ignore_no_migrations\n        self.replace_migrations = replace_migrations\n        if load:\n            self.build_graph()\n\n    @classmethod\n    def migrations_module(cls, app_label):\n        \"\"\"\n        Return the path to the migrations module for the specified app_label\n        and a boolean indicating if the module is specified in\n        settings.MIGRATION_MODULE.\n        \"\"\"\n        if app_label in settings.MIGRATION_MODULES:\n            return settings.MIGRATION_MODULES[app_label], True\n        else:\n            app_package_name = apps.get_app_config(app_label).name\n            return \"%s.%s\" % (app_package_name, MIGRATIONS_MODULE_NAME), False\n\n    def load_disk(self):\n        \"\"\"Load the migrations from all INSTALLED_APPS from disk.\"\"\"\n        self.disk_migrations = {}\n        self.unmigrated_apps = set()\n        self.migrated_apps = set()\n        for app_config in apps.get_app_configs():\n            # Module is not a package (e.g. migrations.py).\n                if not hasattr(module, \"__path__\"):\n                    self.unmigrated_apps.add(app_config.label)\n                    continue\n                # Empty directories are namespaces. Namespace packages have no\n                # __file__ and don't use a list for __path__. See\n                # https://docs.python.org/3/reference/import.html#namespace-packages\n                if getattr(module, \"__file__\", None) is None and not isinstance(\n                    module.__path__, list\n                ):\n                    self.unmigrated_apps.add(app_config.label)\n                    continue\n                # Special-case __first__, which means \"the first migration\" for\n        # migrated apps, and is ignored for unmigrated apps. It allows\n        # makemigrations to declare dependencies on apps before they even have\n        # migrations.\n        if key[0] == current_app:\n            # Ignore __first__ references to the same app (#22325)\n            return\n        if key[0] in self.unmigrated_apps:\n            # Called before but not finished the replacement, this means there\n            # is a circular dependency.\n            raise CommandError(\n                f\"Cyclical squash replacement found, starting at {migration_key}\"\n            )\n        self.replacements_progress[migration_key] = False\n        migration = self.replacements[migration_key]\n        # Process potential squashed migrations that the migration replaces.\n        for replace_migration_key in migration.replaces:\n            if replace_migration_key in self.replacements:\n                self.replace_migration(replace_migration_key)\n\n        replaced_keys = self._resolve_replaced_migration_keys(migration)\n        # Get applied status of each found replacement target.\n        applied_statuses = [\n            (target in self.applied_migrations) for target in replaced_keys\n        ]\n        # The replacing migration is only marked as applied if all of its\n        # A replacing migration can be used if either all or none of its\n        # replacement targets have been applied.\n        if all(applied_statuses) or (not any(applied_statuses)):\n            self.graph.remove_replaced_nodes(migration_key, migration.replaces)\n        else:\n            # This replacing migration cannot be used because it is\n            # partially applied. Remove it from the graph and remap\n            # dependencies to it (#25945).\n            self.graph.remove_replacement_node(migration_key, migration.replaces)\n\n        self.replacements_progress[migration_key] = True\n\n    def build_graph(self):\n        \"\"\"\n        Build a migration dependency graph using both the disk and database.\n        You'll need to rebuild the graph if you apply migrations. This isn't\n        usually a problem as generally migration stuff runs in a one-shot\n        process.\n        \"\"\"\n        # Load disk data\n        self.load_disk()\n        # Load database data\n        if self.connection is None:\n            self.applied_migrations = {}\n        else:\n            recorder = MigrationRecorder(self.connection)\n            self.applied_migrations = recorder.applied_migrations()\n        # To start, populate the migration graph with nodes for ALL migrations\n        # and their dependencies. Also make note of replacing migrations at\n        # this step.\n        self.graph = MigrationGraph()\n        self.replacements = {}\n        for key, migration in self.disk_migrations.items():\n            self.graph.add_node(key, migration)\n            # Replacing migrations.\n            if migration.replaces:\n                self.replacements[key] = migration\n        for key, migration in self.disk_migrations.items():\n            # Internal (same app) dependencies.\n            self.add_internal_dependencies(key, migration)\n        # Add external dependencies now that the internal ones have been\n        # resolved.\n        for key, migration in self.disk_migrations.items():\n            self.add_external_dependencies(key, migration)\n        # Carry out replacements where possible and if enabled.\n        if self.replace_migrations:\n            self.replacements_progress = {}\n            for migration_key in self.replacements.keys():\n                self.replace_migration(migration_key)\n        # Ensure the graph is consistent.\n        try:\n            self.graph.validate_consistency()\n        except NodeNotFoundError as exc:\n            # Check if the missing node could have been replaced by any squash\n            # migration but wasn't because the squash migration was partially\n            # applied before. In that case raise a more understandable\n            # exception (#23556).\n            # Get reverse replacements.\n            reverse_replacements = {}\n            for key, migration in self.replacements.items():\n                for replaced in migration.replaces:\n                    reverse_replacements.setdefault(replaced, set()).add(key)\n            # If the migration is unknown, skip it.\n            if migration not in self.graph.nodes:\n                continue\n            for parent in self.graph.node_map[migration].parents:\n                if parent not in applied:\n                    # Skip unapplied squashed migrations that have all of their\n                    # `replaces` applied.\n                    if self.all_replaced_applied(parent.key, applied):\n                        continue\n                    raise InconsistentMigrationHistory(\n                        \"Migration {}.{} is applied before its dependency \"\n                        \"{}.{} on database '{}'.\".format(\n                            migration[0],\n                            migration[1],\n                            parent[0],\n                            parent[1],\n                            connection.alias,\n                        )\n                    )\n\n    def all_replaced_applied(self, migration_key, applied):\n        \"\"\"\n        Checks (recursively) whether all replaced migrations are applied.\n        \"\"\"\n        if migration_key in self.replacements:\n            for replaced_key in self.replacements[migration_key].replaces:\n                if replaced_key not in applied and not self.all_replaced_applied(\n                    replaced_key, applied\n                ):\n                    return False\n            return True\n\n        return False\n\n    def detect_conflicts(self):\n        \"\"\"\n        Look through the loaded graph and detect any conflicts - apps\n        with more than one leaf migration. Return a dict of the app labels\n        that conflict with the migration names that conflict.\n        \"\"\"\n        seen_apps = {}\n        conflicting_apps = set()\n        for app_label, migration_name in self.graph.leaf_nodes():\n            if app_label in seen_apps:\n                conflicting_apps.add(app_label)\n            seen_apps.setdefault(app_label, set()).add(migration_name)\n        return {\n            app_label: sorted(seen_apps[app_label]) for app_label in conflicting_apps\n        }\n\n    def project_state(self, nodes=None, at_end=True):\n        \"\"\"\n        Return a ProjectState object representing the most recent state\n        that the loaded migrations represent.\n\n        See graph.make_state() for the meaning of \"nodes\" and \"at_end\".\n        \"\"\"\n        return self.graph.make_state(\n            nodes=nodes, at_end=at_end, real_apps=self.unmigrated_apps\n        )\n\n    def collect_sql(self, plan):\n        \"\"\"\n        Take a migration plan and return a list of collected SQL statements\n        that represent the best-efforts version of that plan.\n        \"\"\"\n        statements = []\n        state = None\n        for migration, backwards in plan:\n            with self.connection.schema_editor(\n                collect_sql=True, atomic=migration.atomic\n            ) as schema_editor:\n                if state is None:\n                    state = self.project_state(\n                        (migration.app_label, migration.name), at_end=False\n                    )\n                if not backwards:\n                    state = migration.apply(state, schema_editor, collect_sql=True)\n                else:\n                    state = migration.unapply(state, schema_editor, collect_sql=True)\n            statements.extend(schema_editor.collected_sql)\n        return statements\n","numLines":434,"startLine":1,"totalLines":434}}}

Create the forwards plan Django would follow on an empty database\n            full_plan = self.migration_plan(\n                self.loader.graph.leaf_nodes(), clean_start=True\n            )\n            applied_migrations = {\n                self.loader.graph.nodes[key]\n                for key in self.loader.applied_migrations\n                if key in self.loader.graph.nodes\n            }\n            for migration, _ in full_plan:\n                if migration in applied_migrations:\n                    migration.mutate_state(state, preserve=False)\n        return state\n\n    def migrate(self, targets, plan=None, state=None, fake=False, fake_initial=False):\n        \"\"\"\n        Migrate the database up to the given targets.\n\n        Django first needs to create all project states before a migration is\n        (un)applied and in a second step run all the database operations.\n        \"\"\"\n        # The django_migrations table must be present to record applied\n        # migrations, but don't create it if there are no migrations to apply.\n        if plan == []:\n            if not self.recorder.has_table():\n                return self._create_project_state(with_applied_migrations=False)\n        else:\n            self.recorder.ensure_schema()\n\n        if plan is None:\n            plan = self.migration_plan(targets)\n        # Create the forwards plan Django would follow on an empty database\n        full_plan = self.migration_plan(\n            self.loader.graph.leaf_nodes(), clean_start=True\n        )\n\n        all_forwards = all(not backwards for mig, backwards in plan)\n        all_backwards = all(backwards for mig, backwards in plan)\n\n        if not plan:\n            if state is None:\n                # The resulting state should include applied migrations.\n                state = self._create_project_state(with_applied_migrations=True)\n        elif all_forwards == all_backwards:\n            # This should only happen if there's a mixed plan\n            raise InvalidMigrationPlan(\n                \"Migration plans with both forwards and backwards migrations \"\n                \"are not supported. Please split your migration process into \"\n                \"separate plans of only forwards OR backwards migrations.\",\n                plan,\n            )\n        elif all_forwards:\n            if state is None:\n                # The resulting state should still include applied migrations.\n                state = self._create_project_state(with_applied_migrations=True)\n            state = self._migrate_all_forwards(\n                state, plan, full_plan, fake=fake, fake_initial=fake_initial\n            )\n        else:\n            # No need to check for `elif all_backwards` here, as that condition\n            # would always evaluate to true.\n            state = self._migrate_all_backwards(plan, full_plan, fake=fake)\n\n        self.check_replacements()\n\n        return state\n\n    def _migrate_all_forwards(self, state, plan, full_plan, fake, fake_initial):\n        \"\"\"\n        Take a list of 2-tuples of the form (migration instance, False) and\n        apply them in the order they occur in the full_plan.\n        \"\"\"\n        migrations_to_run = {m[0] for m in plan}\n        for migration, _ in full_plan:\n            if not migrations_to_run:\n                # We remove every migration that we applied from these sets so\n                # that we can bail out once the last migration has been applied\n                # and don't always run until the very end of the migration\n                # process.\n                break\n            if migration in migrations_to_run:\n                if \"apps\" not in state.__dict__:\n                    if self.progress_callback:\n                        self.progress_callback(\"render_start\")\n                    state.apps  # Render all -- performance critical\n                    if self.progress_callback:\n                        self.progress_callback(\"render_success\")\n                state = self.apply_migration(\n                    state, migration, fake=fake, fake_initial=fake_initial\n                )\n                migrations_to_run.remove(migration)\n\n        return state\n\n    def _migrate_all_backwards(self, plan, full_plan, fake):\n        \"\"\"\n        Take a list of 2-tuples of the form (migration instance, True) and\n        unapply them in reverse order they occur in the full_plan.\n\n        Since unapplying a migration requires the project state prior to that\n        migration, Django will compute the migration states before each of them\n        in a first run over the plan and then unapply them in a second run over\n        the plan.\n        \"\"\"\n        migrations_to_run = {m[0] for m in plan}\n        # Holds all migration states prior to the migrations being unapplied\n        states = {}\n        state = self._create_project_state()\n        applied_migrations = {\n            self.loader.graph.nodes[key]\n            for key in self.loader.applied_migrations\n            if key in self.loader.graph.nodes\n        }\n        if self.progress_callback:\n            self.progress_callback(\"render_start\")\n        for migration, _ in full_plan:\n            if not migrations_to_run:\n                # We remove every migration that we applied from this set so\n                # that we can bail out once the last migration has been applied\n                # and don't always run until the very end of the migration\n                # process.\n                break\n            if migration in migrations_to_run:\n                if \"apps\" not in state.__dict__:\n                    state.apps  # Render all -- performance critical\n                # The state before this migration\n                states[migration] = state\n                # The old state keeps as-is, we continue with the new state\n                state = migration.mutate_state(state, preserve=True)\n                migrations_to_run.remove(migration)\n            elif migration in applied_migrations:\n                # Only mutate the state if the migration is actually applied\n                # to make sure the resulting state doesn't include changes\n                # from unrelated migrations.\n                migration.mutate_state(state, preserve=False)\n        if self.progress_callback:\n            self.progress_callback(\"render_success\")\n\n        for migration, _ in plan:\n            self.unapply_migration(states[migration], migration, fake=fake)\n            applied_migrations.remove(migration)\n\n        # Generate the post migration state by starting from the state before\n        # the last migration is unapplied and mutating it to include all the\n        # remaining applied migrations.\n        last_unapplied_migration = plan[-1][0]\n        state = states[last_unapplied_migration]\n        # Avoid mutating state with apps rendered as it's an expensive\n        # operation.\n        del state.apps\n        for index, (migration, _) in enumerate(full_plan):\n            if migration == last_unapplied_migration:\n                for migration, _ in full_plan[index:]:\n                    if migration in applied_migrations:\n                        migration.mutate_state(state, preserve=False)\n                break\n\n        return state\n\n    def apply_migration(self, state, migration, fake=False, fake_initial=False):\n        \"\"\"Run a migration forwards.\"\"\"\n        migration_recorded = False\n        if self.progress_callback:\n            self.progress_callback(\"apply_start\", migration, fake)\n        if not fake:\n            if fake_initial:\n                # Test to see if this is an already-applied initial migration\n                applied, state = self.detect_soft_applied(state, migration)\n                if applied:\n                    fake = True\n            if not fake:\n                # Alright, do it normally\n                with self.connection.schema_editor(\n                    atomic=migration.atomic\n                ) as schema_editor:\n                    state = migration.apply(state, schema_editor)\n                    if not schema_editor.deferred_sql:\n                        self.record_migration(migration.app_label, migration.name)\n                        migration_recorded = True\n        if not migration_recorded:\n            self.record_migration(migration.app_label, migration.name)\n        # Report progress\n        if self.progress_callback:\n            self.progress_callback(\"apply_success\", migration, fake)\n        return state\n\n    def record_migration(self, app_label, name, forward=True):\n        migration = self.loader.disk_migrations.get((app_label, name))\n        # For replacement migrations, record individual statuses\n        if migration and migration.replaces:\n            for replaced_app_label, replaced_name in migration.replaces:\n                self.record_migration(replaced_app_label, replaced_name, forward)\n        if forward:\n            self.recorder.record_applied(app_label, name)\n        else:\n            self.recorder.record_unapplied(app_label, name)\n\n    def unapply_migration(self, state, migration, fake=False):\n        \"\"\"Run a migration backwards.\"\"\"\n        if self.progress_callback:\n            self.progress_callback(\"unapply_start\", migration, fake)\n        if not fake:\n            with self.connection.schema_editor(\n                atomic=migration.atomic\n            ) as schema_editor:\n                state = migration.unapply(state, schema_editor)\n        self.record_migration(migration.app_label, migration.name, forward=False)\n        # Report progress\n        if self.progress_callback:\n            self.progress_callback(\"unapply_success\", migration, fake)\n        return state\n\n    def check_replacements(self):\n        \"\"\"\n        Mark replacement migrations applied if their replaced set all are.\n\n        Do this unconditionally on every migrate, rather than just when\n        migrations are applied or unapplied, to correctly handle the case\n        when a new squash migration is pushed to a deployment that already had\n        all its replaced migrations applied. In this case no new migration will\n        be applied, but the applied state of the squashed migration must be\n        maintained.\n        \"\"\"\n        applied = self.recorder.applied_migrations()\n        for key, migration in self.loader.replacements.items():\n            if key not in applied and self.loader.all_replaced_applied(key, applied):\n                self.recorder.record_applied(*key)\n\n    def detect_soft_applied(self, project_state, migration):\n        \"\"\"\n        Test whether a migration has been implicitly applied - that the\n        tables or columns it would create exist. This is intended only for use\n        on initial migrations (as it only looks for CreateModel and AddField).\n        \"\"\"\n\n        def should_skip_detecting_model(migration, model):\n            \"\"\"\n            No need to detect tables for proxy models, unmanaged models, or\n            models that can't be migrated on the current database.\n            \"\"\"\n            return (\n                model._meta.proxy\n                or not model._meta.managed\n                or not router.allow_migrate(\n                    self.connection.alias,\n                    migration.app_label,\n                    model_name=model._meta.model_name,\n                )\n            )\n\n        if migration.initial is None:\n            # Bail if the migration isn't the first one in its app\n            if any(app == migration.app_label for app, name in migration.dependencies):\n                return False, project_state\n        elif migration.initial is False:\n            # Bail if it's NOT an initial migration\n            return False, project_state\n\n        if project_state is None:\n            after_state = self.loader.project_state(\n                (migration.app_label, migration.name), at_end=True\n            )\n        else:\n            after_state = migration.mutate_state(project_state)\n        apps = after_state.apps\n        found_create_model_migration = False\n        found_add_field_migration = False\n        fold_identifier_case = self.connection.features.ignores_table_name_case\n        with self.connection.cursor() as cursor:\n            existing_table_names = set(\n                self.connection.introspection.table_names(cursor)\n            )\n            if fold_identifier_case:\n                existing_table_names = {\n                    name.casefold() for name in existing_table_names\n                }\n        # Make sure all create model and add field operations are done\n        for operation in migration.operations:\n            if isinstance(operation, migrations.CreateModel):\n                model = apps.get_model(migration.app_label, operation.name)\n                if model._meta.swapped:\n                    # We have to fetch the model to test with from the\n                    # main app cache, as it's not a direct dependency.\n                    model = global_apps.get_model(model._meta.swapped)\n                if should_skip_detecting_model(migration, model):\n                    continue\n                db_table = model._meta.db_table\n                if fold_identifier_case:\n                    db_table = db_table.casefold()\n                if db_table not in existing_table_names:\n                    return False, project_state\n                found_create_model_migration = True\n            elif isinstance(operation, migrations.AddField):\n                model = apps.get_model(migration.app_label, operation.model_name)\n                if model._meta.swapped:\n                    # We have to fetch the model to test with from the\n                    # main app cache, as it's not a direct dependency.\n                    model = global_apps.get_model(model._meta.swapped)\n                if should_skip_detecting_model(migration, model):\n                    continue\n\n                table = model._meta.db_table\n                field = model._meta.get_field(operation.name)\n\n                # Handle implicit many-to-many tables created by AddField.\n                if field.many_to_many:\n                    through_db_table = field.remote_field.through._meta.db_table\n                    if fold_identifier_case:\n                        through_db_table = through_db_table.casefold()\n                    if through_db_table not in existing_table_names:\n                        return False, project_state\n                    else:\n                        found_add_field_migration = True\n                        continue\n                with self.connection.cursor() as cursor:\n                    columns = self.connection.introspection.get_table_description(\n                        cursor, table\n                    )\n                for column in columns:\n                    field_column = field.column\n                    column_name = column.name\n                    if fold_identifier_case:\n                        column_name = column_name.casefold()\n                        field_column = field_column.casefold()\n                    if column_name == field_column:\n                        found_add_field_migration = True\n                        break\n                else:\n                    return False, project_state\n        # sometimes a single-level\n        deconstruction will not compare correctly.\n        \"\"\"\n        if isinstance(obj, list):\n            return [self.deep_deconstruct(value) for value in obj]\n        elif isinstance(obj, tuple):\n            return tuple(self.deep_deconstruct(value) for value in obj)\n        elif isinstance(obj, dict):\n            return {key: self.deep_deconstruct(value) for key, value in obj.items()}\n        elif isinstance(obj, functools.partial):\n            return (\n                obj.func,\n                self.deep_deconstruct(obj.args),\n                self.deep_deconstruct(obj.keywords),\n            )\n        elif isinstance(obj, COMPILED_REGEX_TYPE):\n            return RegexObject(obj)\n        elif isinstance(obj, type):\n            # If this is a type that implements 'deconstruct' as an instance\n            # method, avoid treating this as being deconstructible itself - see\n            # #22951\n            return obj\n        elif hasattr(obj, \"deconstruct\"):\n            deconstructed = obj.deconstruct()\n            if isinstance(obj, models.Field):\n                # we have a field which also returns a name\n                deconstructed = deconstructed[1:]\n            path, args, kwargs = deconstructed\n            return (\n                path,\n                [self.deep_deconstruct(value) for value in args],\n                {key: self.deep_deconstruct(value) for key, value in kwargs.items()},\n            )\n        else:\n            return obj\n\n    def only_relation_agnostic_fields(self, fields):\n        \"\"\"\n        Return a definition of the fields that ignores field names and\n        what related fields actually relate to. The dict has app labels\n        as keys and a list of migrations as values.\n\n        The resulting migrations aren't specially named, but the names\n        do matter for dependencies inside the set.\n\n        convert_apps is the list of apps to convert to use migrations\n        (i.e. to make initial migrations for, in the usual case)\n\n        graph is an optional argument that, if provided, can help improve\n        dependency generation and avoid potential circular dependencies.\n        \"\"\"\n        # The first phase is generating all the operations for each app\n        # and gathering them into a big per-app list.\n        # Then go through that list, order it, and split into migrations to\n        # resolve dependencies caused by M2Ms and FKs.\n        self.generated_operations = {}\n        self.altered_indexes = {}\n        self.altered_constraints = {}\n        self.renamed_fields = {}\n","numLines":150,"startLine":1,"totalLines":2067}}}

in the django/db/migrations/ directory and the django/core/management/commands/ directory.\\n\\n**1. Squash Migration Generator (django/core/management/commands/squashmigrations.py):**\\nThe Command class implements the \\\"squashmigrations\\\" management command that generates squashed migrations. The handle() method orchestrates the squashing process by: (1) loading the migration graph, (2) identifying migrations to squash, (3) collecting their operations and dependencies, (4) optionally optimizing operations via MigrationOptimizer, and (5) creating a new Migration subclass with a 'replaces' attribute listing all squashed migrations.\\n\\n**2. Replaced-Migrations Tracking (django/db/migrations/loader.py):**\\nThe MigrationLoader class manages replaced migrations. Key methods include: _resolve_replaced_migration_keys() which recursively resolves all replaced migrations including those replaced by other squashed migrations; replace_migration() which processes replacement migrations and detects cyclical squash replacements by tracking progress state; all_replaced_applied() which recursively checks whether all replaced migrations are applied to the database; and build_graph() which populates the self.replacements dictionary and applies replacement logic when replace_migrations=True.\\n\\n**3. Dependency Graph Validation After Squashing (django/db/migrations/graph.py):**\\nThe MigrationGraph class manages the migration dependency graph with methods for handling squashed migrations: remove_replaced_nodes() removes replaced migration nodes from the graph and redirects dependencies from replaced nodes to the replacement node; remove_replacement_node() does the inverse when a replacement cannot be used (partial application); validate_consistency() ensures no DummyNode instances remain in the graph (representing missing dependencies); ensure_not_cyclic() detects circular dependencies using depth-first search; and forwards_plan()/backwards_plan() traverse dependencies correctly through replaced and replacement nodes.\\n\\n**4. Squash Completeness Check (django/db/migrations/executor.py and django/db/migrations/migration.py):**\\nThe MigrationExecutor.check_replacements() method marks replacement migrations as applied if all their replaced migrations are applied, handling the case where a new squash migration is pushed after old migrations already exist. The Migration class defines a 'replaces' attribute (list of migration tuples) which is serialized by MigrationWriter. The record_migration() method in MigrationExecutor records individual replaced migration status when a replacement migration is applied, ensuring migration history consistency.\\n\\n**Exception Handling:**\\nCircularDependencyError is raised by ensure_not_cyclic() when cycles are detected; NodeNotFoundError is raised when dependency nodes cannot be found; CommandError with message \\\"Cyclical squash replacement found\\\" is raised by replace_migration() when circular replacements are detected; and InconsistentMigrationHistory is raised by check_consistent_history() when applied migrations have unapplied dependencies (with special handling for squashed migrations via all_replaced_applied()).\"\n}\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":11,"cache_creation_input_tokens":1590,"cache_read_input_tokens":57851,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":1590},"output_tokens":3,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"eebe546b-63b0-4347-aef0-d9a014f34f4c","uuid":"78b79374-d33f-491e-ab14-41b94a8b72b0"}

multiple files in the django/db/migrations/ directory and the django/core/management/commands/ directory.\\n\\n**1. Squash Migration Generator (django/core/management/commands/squashmigrations.py):**\\nThe Command class implements the \\\"squashmigrations\\\" management command that generates squashed migrations. The handle() method orchestrates the squashing process by: (1) loading the migration graph, (2) identifying migrations to squash, (3) collecting their operations and dependencies, (4) optionally optimizing operations via MigrationOptimizer, and (5) creating a new Migration subclass with a 'replaces' attribute listing all squashed migrations.\\n\\n**2. Replaced-Migrations Tracking (django/db/migrations/loader.py):**\\nThe MigrationLoader class manages replaced migrations. Key methods include: _resolve_replaced_migration_keys() which recursively resolves all replaced migrations including those replaced by other squashed migrations; replace_migration() which processes replacement migrations and detects cyclical squash replacements by tracking progress state; all_replaced_applied() which recursively checks whether all replaced migrations are applied to the database; and build_graph() which populates the self.replacements dictionary and applies replacement logic when replace_migrations=True.\\n\\n**3. Dependency Graph Validation After Squashing (django/db/migrations/graph.py):**\\nThe MigrationGraph class manages the migration dependency graph with methods for handling squashed migrations: remove_replaced_nodes() removes replaced migration nodes from the graph and redirects dependencies from replaced nodes to the replacement node; remove_replacement_node() does the inverse when a replacement cannot be used (partial application); validate_consistency() ensures no DummyNode instances remain in the graph (representing missing dependencies); ensure_not_cyclic() detects circular dependencies using depth-first search; and forwards_plan()/backwards_plan() traverse dependencies correctly through replaced and replacement nodes.\\n\\n**4. Squash Completeness Check (django/db/migrations/executor.py and django/db/migrations/migration.py):**\\nThe MigrationExecutor.check_replacements() method marks replacement migrations as applied if all their replaced migrations are applied, handling the case where a new squash migration is pushed after old migrations already exist. The Migration class defines a 'replaces' attribute (list of migration tuples) which is serialized by MigrationWriter. The record_migration() method in MigrationExecutor records individual replaced migration status when a replacement migration is applied, ensuring migration history consistency.\\n\\n**Exception Handling:**\\nCircularDependencyError is raised by ensure_not_cyclic() when cycles are detected; NodeNotFoundError is raised when dependency nodes cannot be found; CommandError with message \\\"Cyclical squash replacement found\\\" is raised by replace_migration() when circular replacements are detected; and InconsistentMigrationHistory is raised by check_consistent_history() when applied migrations have unapplied dependencies (with special handling for squashed migrations via all_replaced_applied()).\"\n    55→}\n    56→\n\n<system-reminder>\nWhenever you read a file, you should consider whether it would be considered malware.
